# Kuku Yalanji Dictionary

A complete word list for **Kuku Yalanji**, an Aboriginal language of the rainforest region of far north Queensland, Australia.

**2,287 distinct headwords** across **2,688 entries** (some headwords have several senses, listed separately).

> Generated from [`dictionary.yaml`](dictionary.yaml) by [`gen_markdown.py`](gen_markdown.py). The companion grammar reference is [`grammar.md`](grammar.md). Quoted example sentences are kept as recorded in the source.

## Index

[A](#a) · [B](#b) · [D](#d) · [G](#g) · [J](#j) · [K](#k) · [L](#l) · [M](#m) · [N](#n) · [R](#r) · [U](#u) · [W](#w) · [Y](#y) · [Z](#z)

## A

### aybi  /ˈajbi/  *noun*

- Ivy; an English personal name adapted to Kuku Yalanji phonology

**English:** Ivy (name)  
**Domain:** personal name  
**Loanword:** &lt; English *English 'Ivy'*  
- 📝 *Attested in Patz §2.3 (i) as a phonologically adapted English loan name; not in the source dictionary.*
- 📝 *Shows loan adaptation where /b/ corresponds to English /v/ (Ivy -> aybi).*
- 📝 *Added from the reference grammar (Patz); not present in the original community dictionary.*

### ba  /ˈba/  *intransitive verb*

- come. Baby talk, usually used with very small children only. Used only as a command.

**English:** come  
**Domain:** motion travel  
- 📝 *Baby talk register: per the definition, used only with very small children and only as a command.*

> *Ngayu nyungundu babajin, Wanju nyulu?* — I asked him, Who is he?

**English:** ask, asked  
**Domain:** speech communication  
**Conjugation:** y-conjugation · -ji- (reflexive / general intransitive)

- taste

> *ngayu baduriji dungaka, yinya bubu babanka* — I want to go fishing to try the place out

**English:** try, taste

**English:** young cassowary

### babi  /ˈbabi/  *noun*

- grandmother, father's mother
- grandfather, mother's father

> *Babingka jija kujin-kujil* — Grand mother is looking after her grandchild

**English:** grandmother, grandfather  
**Domain:** kinship  
- 📝 *Polysemous kin term: father's mother (grandmother) and mother's father (grandfather).*

### Babu walu-yindu wawubjaburr Bloomfieldmundurr jalunmun wangkar Binda-babaranga  *intransitive verb*

*Kuwa wawubajaburr wujal-wujaldarr*

**Domain:** speech communication  
- 📝 *This is a full example sentence, not a lexical headword. It contains the place names Bloomfield (with -mundurr) and Binda-babara (locative Binda-babaranga), and verbal material (wangka- 'speak/talk', wawu- 'want/desire').*

### badi  /ˈbadi/  *intransitive verb*

- to cry
- to wail, mourn
- to sing
- to howl

> *karrakay badin mayika* — the child cried for food
> *jana banbadi yaba wulanya* — They are wailing because their older brother died
> *Dikal yalibalaku banbadin* — The birds were singing early in the morning
> *kaya-kaya banbadin majangka bawanya* — the dogs were howling because their master left them

**English:** cry, wail, sing, howl  
**Domain:** cognition emotion  
- 📝 *Semantic range spans crying, wailing/mourning, singing, and howling.*

### baja  /ˈbaɟa/  *adverb*

- again
- more
- I don't know

> *jana kuljubu jarba kunin baja, kunin baja* — They hit the snake again and again with stones
> *yundu wunay baja?* — do you have more?
> *ngayu wanyu baja balkal* — I don't know what to tell

**English:** more, again  
**Domain:** manner  
**Usage:** This is used only with a question word

### bajaku  /ˈbaɟaɡu/  *adverb*

- very
- definitely
- shows intensity

> *jana mayi jirray ajaku manin storemun* — They got very much food from the store
> *ngayu kari bajakudungay* — I'm definitely not going
> *nyulu bama bajaku* — he's a real aboriginal

**English:** very, definitely, real  
**Domain:** manner  
- 📝 *Intensifier marking degree/certainty per the definition (very, definitely, shows intensity).*

### bajalji  /ˈbaɟalɟi/  *noun*

- species of rock python. Not many at Bloomfield, but many at Helenvale, Rossville and Shiptons Flats. They have a white head and will chase bald-headed people not wearing a hat beecause they think they are being copied

**English:** rock python  
**Domain:** fauna reptile  
- 📝 *Distribution noted in prose: few at Bloomfield, many at Helenvale, Rossville and Shiptons Flats.*
- 📝 *Associated lore: white-headed python said to chase bald-headed people not wearing a hat.*

### bama  /ˈbama/  *noun*

- people, mankind
- mankind
- aborigine, not a white person

**English:** people, bama  
**Domain:** human generic classifier  
- 📝 *Definition contrasts bama 'Aboriginal person / mankind' with a white person; the central self-referential term for people in Kuku Yalanji.*

**English:** my word, my voice  
**Domain:** interjection  
- 📝 *Compound: bama 'person/people' + ngayku- '(my)'; an emphatic interjection 'my word'.*

- boys from the time they are babies - ngawa - to older boys - warru

**English:** boys

- 📝 *Definition frames a male age class spanning babies (ngawa) to older boys (warru).*

### dabu  /ˈdabu/  *noun*

- small black bee which nests in trees, has a light sting
- the honey from this bee
- the name of one of the clan moieties

**English:** bee  
**Domain:** fauna insect  
- 📝 *Polysemous: (1) a small black stingless bee; (2) the honey from this bee; (3) the name of one of the clan moieties (cf. dabuy, listed as totem of dabu and walarr moieties at index 504).*

### dabul  /ˈdabul/  *noun*


### dabul  /ˈdabul/  *noun*

- pierced nose and nose peg. The piecing is always done by a man's biwul, his mother in law. Biwulungku dabul bakan. "My mother in law pierced his nose"
- place name - between upper Daintree River and Roaring Meg. The big rock here is a jarramali (thunder) and nose piecing story site.

**English:** pierced nose  
**Domain:** body part  
- 📝 *Definition also records dabul as a place name between the upper Daintree River and Roaring Meg, a nose-piercing story site associated with jarramali (thunder).*
- 📝 *Cultural note in prose: nose piercing is always performed by a man's biwul (mother-in-law). Example sentence: 'Biwulungku dabul bakan' — "My mother in law pierced his nose" (biwul + ergative -ngku).*

### dabulkurra  /ˈdabulɡura/  *noun*

- human shin bone, for conveying messages to someone. The hollow bone is also used to catch a person's shadow which is then closed up inside the bone. This is then used to put withcraft on the person. He may also put a person's urine or other belonging inside.

**English:** shin bone  
**Domain:** body part  
- 📝 *Gloss is the human shin bone; prose records its ceremonial/sorcery use for message-conveying and shadow-catching witchcraft.*

### daburri  /ˈdaburi/  *noun*

- brackish swamp water

**English:** swamp  
**Domain:** water  
- 📝 *Specifically brackish swamp water.*

### dabuy  /ˈdabuj/  *noun*

- small brownish kingfisher, totem of both dabu and walarr moieties. When this bird starts singing yo know you will get company, that someone is travelling.
- spirit

**English:** spirit, kingfisher  
**Domain:** spirit mythical being  
- 📝 *Polysemous: (1) a small brownish kingfisher, totem of both the dabu and walarr moieties, whose singing signals approaching company/travellers; (2) spirit.*

**English:** a directional sign, a sign post, a wreath  
**Domain:** artefact  
- 📝 *A placed directional sign (heap of stones / twisted grass) and a carrying-ring/wreath of soft material; both are made objects.*

## G

### gilaja  *noun*

- glass; a mirror

**English:** glass, mirror  
**Domain:** artefact  
**Loanword:** &lt; English *glass*  
- 📝 *Attested in Patz §2.3(iv),(viii) as a phonologically adapted English loanword; the variant gilaji 'glass' is also recorded in §2.3(viii)(a).*
- 📝 *Loan from English 'glass': the consonant cluster /gl/ is broken up by an epenthetic vowel (§2.3(iv)) and the final consonant adapted by adding a vowel (§2.3(viii)).*
- 📝 *Not in the source dictionary.*
- 📝 *Added from the reference grammar (Patz); not present in the original community dictionary.*

**Domain:** cognition emotion  
- 📝 *Attested in Patz §4.2.4.4: 'Janjarri-l "laugh about, ridicule" and janjarriji-y "laugh at in a friendly way" can probably also be included in this list [of fixed intransitive stems].'*
- 📝 *Patz explicitly regards such -ji-y forms as 'fixed' intransitive stems with meaning shifted from the transitive base, not as productive antipassives; hence dictionary-worthy as its own lexeme.*
- 📝 *Not in the source dictionary.*
- 📝 *Added from the reference grammar (Patz); not present in the original community dictionary.*

### jingajalka  /ˈɟiŋaɟalɡa/  *noun*

- species of tree, also its edible fruit, which is small and elongated and plum-like with a large seed. The tree has bark out of which baskets can be made. It peels off easily then is put into the fire for a minute to soften, then it is bent and the ends tied to form a basket. It is used to cook with - hot stones can also be put in the water in it - and it was used to carry bones of the dead.

**English:** tree, jingajalka  
**Domain:** flora tree  
- 📝 *Prose details extensive cultural use: bark peeled and softened in fire to form baskets used for cooking (with hot stones) and to carry bones of the dead.*

- 📝 *Place-name for Collin's Hill.*

### jungur  /ˈɟuŋuɻ/  *noun*


### jungur  /ˈɟuŋuɻ/  *noun*

- the big hill at the east side of the mouth of the Bloomfield River. Collins Hill (place name)

**English:** Collins Hill, jungur  
**Domain:** place name  
- 📝 *Definition explicitly marks it as a place name: the big hill at the east of the Bloomfield River mouth (Collins Hill).*

### junjun  /ˈɟunɟun/  *noun*

- species of wild fruit, ripe in March - May. During the junjun season, the scrub turkey, which normally lives in the high country, will come down to feed on them

**English:** wild fruit, junjun  
**Domain:** flora plant  
**Reduplication:** full (base *jun*)  
- 📝 *Species of wild fruit ripening March-May; definition notes scrub turkeys descend from high country to feed during junjun season.*

### junjuy  /ˈɟunɟuj/  *noun*

**English:** something, nothing  
**Domain:** value quality  
- 📝 *Glossed 'something, usually of no value'.*

**Domain:** value quality  
**Reduplication:** full (base *junjuy*)  
- 📝 *Reduplication of junjuy (1140), glossed 'things'.*

### kanunjul  /ˈɡanunɟul/  *noun*

- resin of grass tree, used to make pitch to seal spear bindings. Also used in the control of thunder storms, as is nganjirr and jujabala and kangka. Kanunjul is also used to smoke the inside of a house after the owner dies.

**English:** resin of grass tree, pitch, seal spear bindings, smoke the inside of a house after the owner dies  
**Domain:** flora plant  
**Synonyms:** nganjirr  
- 📝 *Resin of grass tree, used as pitch to seal spear bindings; prose notes ritual use in thunderstorm control (alongside nganjirr, jujabala, kangka) and for smoking a house after the owner's death.*

### kanyil  /ˈɡaɲil/  *noun*

- curse song. It is sung by one person against another who has seriously wronged him, i.e. stolen his wife. These songs are greatly feared, and act as a deterrent against wrongdoing.

**Domain:** ceremony magic song  
**Synonyms:** yilal  
**Usage:** {'english': 'to sing a curse song', 'translation': 'kanyil badi'}

### karangal  /ˈɡaɻaŋal/  *intransitive verb*

**Conjugation:** l-conjugation · -bunga-l (state-causative)  
- 📝 *Transitive 'to stare', formed with the verbaliser -bungal (cf. kunkun).*

**Conjugation:** l-conjugation  
**Usage:** {'english': 'The man was angry and throwing things around', 'translation': 'Nyulu dingkar kuliji marra-warrin'}; {'english': 'The kids went down river (when a floor was running)', 'translation': 'Jana kaykay-kaykay bada marra-warrin'}  
- 📝 *Polysemous: violent temper tantrum; also heedless/reckless wandering by children.*

**Usage:** {'english': 'They went real fast, the boat made a big splash (bow wave) (as it goes along fast)', 'translation': 'Jana jinbalku dungan, buwunda bana minji-kangan'}; {'english': 'The fire has a lot of flames shooting up', 'translation': 'Baya minijiji'}

- tidy up, make neat, straighten out.

**English:** tidy up, make neat, straighten out  
**Domain:** manipulation impact  
**Conjugation:** l-conjugation  
**Synonyms:** mala, juburr  
**Usage:** {'english': 'He is a good carpenter (does neat work)', 'translation': 'Nyulu minjin-damal bayan'}  
- 📝 *Compound verb; the -damal element is a common transitive verbaliser ('make/do').*

### mirrba  /ˈmirba/  *noun*

- a wooden instrument to help throw spears more powerfully. This was used as an instrument of defence. After being found guilty, a man used to be given a woomera with which to ward off the spears thrown by a group of men. The aim was not to kill except for a capital offence. also rifle

**English:** woomera, rifle  
**Domain:** weapon  
- 📝 *Spear-thrower (woomera) used defensively to ward off thrown spears in judicial duels; sense extended to 'rifle'.*

### miyil  /ˈmijil/  *noun*

### mulkal-mulkal  /ˈmulɡal-mulɡal/  *noun*

- totem. This word spoken with a rising intonation is an enquiry into a person's secret life.
- state of mind to fight for no reason. The father of an unborn child becomes angry at a mate and he will hit the mate at slightest pretense. This is then a sign that his wife is pregnant. Can also be anyone who fights for no reason. This is also a sign someone is pregnant
- the spirit being who keeps a snake from biting a pregnant woman

**English:** totem, state of mind, spirit being, story, background  
**Domain:** spirit mythical being  
**Reduplication:** full (base *mulkal*)  
**Usage:** {'english': "They're fighting for no reason. Someone will have a baby.", 'translation': 'Bula mulkal-mulkal; somebodyngka baby haveim-bungal'}  
- 📝 *Reduplicated form. Prose notes rising intonation turns it into an enquiry into a person's secret life; also denotes a spirit being protecting a pregnant woman from snakebite and a fighting-without-reason state of mind.*

**Usage:** {'english': 'The clothes are hanging on the line', 'translation': 'Kambi walngkal-walngkal lineba'}; {'english': 'The log is floating on the water', 'translation': 'Juku walngkal-walngkal bananga'}  

### walngkan-damal  /ˈwalŋɡan-damal/  *transitive verb*

- to hang up

**English:** to hang up  
**Domain:** manipulation impact  
**Conjugation:** l-conjugation  
**Usage:** {'english': 'The woman hung the clothes up on the line', 'translation': 'Jabungku kambi walngkandaman lineba'}  
- 📝 *Causative/transitive of 'walngkal' (to hang), with the -damal suffix; 'to hang up'.*

### walngkurril  /ˈwalŋɡuril/  *transitive verb*

**Synonyms:** kunjaji

- 📝 *Nyungkul dialect form glossed as to beg/ask for something; also 'bark of a dog'.*

- the spirit of a man
- breath

**English:** soul, essence  
**Domain:** spirit mythical being  
- 📝 *The spirit/soul of a person; also glossed 'breath'.*

### wawu  /ˈwawu/  *transitive verb*

- wish, want, need, love, like

**English:** wish, want, need, love, like  
**Domain:** cognition emotion  
- 📝 *Homophone of wawu 'soul/breath'; here a desiderative meaning wish/want/need/love/like.*

- 📝 *wawu 'soul' + jirray ('big/much'), i.e. to love/like very much.*

### wuyngkul  /ˈwujŋɡul/  *noun*

- spirit of sick person. Only a few people who know the wuynkul can see and talk to him. if they stare at him he hits them with a stick and the next day they become sick. He has eyes in front and behind him, and can see if bama stare at him. He can appear as a person, as a hairy brute with long teeth and a bad smell, or as a wild pig or snake. When by other persons, he has left the sick person.

**English:** spirit, demon, trickster  
**Domain:** spirit mythical being  

### wuyngkulji  /ˈwujŋɡulɟi/  *noun*

- 📝 *Derived from wuyngkul: one possessed by the wuyngkul spirit.*

### yaba  /ˈjaba/  *noun*

- older brother

### yamba  /ˈjamba/  *noun*

- 📝 *Attested in Patz §3.7, Table 3.12 / Table 3.13 (absolutive form of the demonstrative pronoun 'this/these'); also Text 51 line 72, exx.(123),(361),(429),(431),(625),(649). Not in the source dictionary.*
- 📝 *Nyungkul counterpart of Yalanji yanyu; suppletive inflected bases use yala- (e.g. ERG yalabu, DAT yalayngka).*

### yarkin-bunga-l  /ˈjaɻɡin-buŋa-l/  *transitive verb*

- to kill (literally 'make a corpse'); state-causative compound verb

**English:** kill  
**Domain:** manipulation impact  
- 📝 *Attested in Patz §3.8.5.1(i); not in the source dictionary.*
- 📝 *Compound of yarkin 'corpse' (in dictionary) + state-causative verbaliser -bunga-l ('make into N'). l-conjugation. Lexicalised idiomatic meaning 'kill'.*
- 📝 *Added from the reference grammar (Patz); not present in the original community dictionary.*

**Domain:** manner  
- 📝 *Attested in Patz §3.8.6.1 (Manner table of adverbial particles); not in the source dictionary.*
- 📝 *Like other adverbial particles it may take manner suffix -ku and reduplicate, but occurs in simple root form and cannot take case inflection.*
- 📝 *Added from the reference grammar (Patz); not present in the original community dictionary.*

### yurrunji  /ˈjurunɟi/  *noun*

- species of tree, called "dead finish" by whites. It is found only in Kuku-Nyungkul country except for one tree standing all alone at Main camp which is in Kuku-Yalanji country. The story is that he came from Romeo and was in Love with (bujanji) but was rejected and is now standing alone

**English:** tree, dead finish  
**Domain:** flora tree  
- 📝 *Species of tree called 'dead finish' by whites; said to grow only in Kuku-Nyungkul country except one tree at Main camp in Kuku-Yalanji country, with an associated story.*

- 📝 *Compound with yuru- as initial element; to join together by means of something else (nailing, sewing, etc.).*

## Z

### Zigazagmun Main Campmunbu  *locational*

*Zigazagmun Main Campmunbu*

**Domain:** place name  
- 📝 *Capitalised multi-word headword incorporating English 'Main Camp' plus Yalanji locative suffix -munbu, indicating a named place/location.*
